A typical IDA system consists of three core components:\n\n1.  **Host (A):** A molecule possessing a recognition cavity or binding site.\n2.  **Indicator (B):** A guest molecule that exhibits a signal response (e.g., in its color or fluorescence).\n3.  **Analyte (C):** The target guest molecule to be detected.\n\nThe principle of operation involves two steps:\n\n1. This displacement restores the indicator's signal to its original state, thus enabling the detection of the analyte C.\n\n------\n\n**Problem Statement**\n\nA given IDA system consists of the following components:\n\n* **Known Component 1:** TCC: A large macrocyclic host based on a calix[4]arene scaffold, where four phenol-derived units are linked by ether bridges.
